  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dde7ca8c-58db-4cb5-84a8-5d848a0a8d93'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText8779393472493323094" style="display:none">"We have stepped off the cliff and are falling into madness."<br /><br />The mind-bending pace of <i>Black</i> accelerates in <i>Red</i>, Book Two of Ted Dekker's groundbreaking Circle trilogy.<br /><br />Less than a month ago, Thomas Hunter was a failed writer selling coffee at the Java Hut in Denver. Now he finds himself in a desperate quest to rescue two worlds from collapse. In one world, he's a battle-scarred general commanding an army of primitive warriors. In the other, he's racing to outwit sadistic terrorists intent on creating global chaos through an unstoppable virus.<br /><br />Two worlds on the brink of destruction. One unthinkable solution.<br /><br />Enter an adrenaline-laced epic where dreams and reality collide. Nothing is as it seems, as <i>Black</i> turns to <i>Red</i>.</span>

<div id="review_2732513715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732513715" />
    <a title="Sarah Grace Grzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy"><img alt="Sarah Grace Grzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570047933p2/59507807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732513715?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Grace Grzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Grace Grzy" href="/user/show/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy">Sarah Grace Grzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah Grace by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/25563718-micaiah">Micaiah</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732513715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8412909733662277531">W.o.w. I don't think mere words can actually encompass my thoughts about this book, but I will do my best. <br/><br/>This isn't the type of book I usually read, but, at the insistence of several friends, I decided to give this series a shot. A strangely gripping combination of sci-fi, thriller, and fantasy, The Circle series is unlike anything I've ever read, and, I would guess, unparalleled in its genre. (Whatever genre that is.)<br/><br/>First off, any expectations you may have when you start this book, just thro</span>
  <span id="freeText8412909733662277531" style="display:none">W.o.w. I don't think mere words can actually encompass my thoughts about this book, but I will do my best. <br /><br />This isn't the type of book I usually read, but, at the insistence of several friends, I decided to give this series a shot. A strangely gripping combination of sci-fi, thriller, and fantasy, The Circle series is unlike anything I've ever read, and, I would guess, unparalleled in its genre. (Whatever genre that is.)<br /><br />First off, any expectations you may have when you start this book, just throw them out of the window right here and now. Black completely turned my expectations on their head, and not completely in a good way. It was just so different from what I expected that I struggled a bit. Certain elements were so bizarre they were too bizarre for me. <br /><br />That being said, by the time I finished Black, there was no way I could just not read the rest of the series. So I dove into Red. (Quick note: I listened to the audiobook version of Red and highly recommend it. The narrator is fabulous.)<br /><br />Red. What to even say. All the previously high stakes are raised to even higher levels, and you have no idea how anything can turn out right. It was somewhat jarring for me to go from young, naive Thomas in the other world to 40-year-old war hero general Thomas. That was a pretty big jump that took some getting used to, but I grew to love that Thomas just as much as the Thomas in Black. Dekker knows how to do characters well--each and every one is so colorful and unique, and that's one of the main reasons I loved this so much. Note for those who were offended that I didn't like Rachelle in Black, I did like her much better in Red, just so you know. ;)<br /><br />The other reason is the allegory. Wow. While I'm not sure how I feel about the way Dekker portrayed certain allegorical elements, overall he did a fabulous job. Certain elements of the allegory are so incredibly moving I was brought to tears several times. It definitely gave me a new perspective on certain biblical events, which I loved. <br /><br />Speaking of tears, just as it seemed like everything was going to turn out okay, nope, it's not okay. The final twist at the end had me sobbing into my sister's shoulder. Not cool, Dekker. I can't say much because of spoilers, but that end twist was both devastating and moving. Painful, but incredibly well done. <br /><br />Overall, Red is a masterfully written book. It's certainly not for everyone, but I don't think anyone can deny the amount of sheer talent and brilliance it takes to write something like this epic piece of fiction. <br /><br />Now excuse me, I'm off to read White. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="8412909733662277531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_224604831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224604831" />
    <a title="J.S. Bailey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281321-j-s-bailey"><img alt="J.S. Bailey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570121244p2/5281321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224604831?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.S. Bailey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.S. Bailey" href="/user/show/5281321-j-s-bailey">J.S. Bailey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224604831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7338601625665404555">Those who know me in the obscure part of life known to some as "The Real World" know that I do not often express the raging sea of emotions that constantly swirls around inside my brain. Think Jamie Hyneman. Think Mister Spock. Yeah. I'm kinda like them. I'm sure some people think I'm the human equivalent of an android, but that's okay, because they can think whatever they want.<br/><br/>I don't know why I tend to bottle up my emotions. I guess it's just the way I'm made. I spend about 95% of my waking ho</span>
  <span id="freeText7338601625665404555" style="display:none">Those who know me in the obscure part of life known to some as "The Real World" know that I do not often express the raging sea of emotions that constantly swirls around inside my brain. Think Jamie Hyneman. Think Mister Spock. Yeah. I'm kinda like them. I'm sure some people think I'm the human equivalent of an android, but that's okay, because they can think whatever they want.<br /><br />I don't know why I tend to bottle up my emotions. I guess it's just the way I'm made. I spend about 95% of my waking hours alone inside my head anyway, so it only makes sense that my emotions stay put there, too.<br /><br />The reason I'm talking about my emotions is because this book made me shed a tear. Maybe two. I don't know; I didn't count. But you know it takes a lot to do that to someone like me. It happens on occasion with other authors--I got misty-eyed reading Dean Koontz's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14995.Odd_Thomas__Odd_Thomas___1_" title="Odd Thomas (Odd Thomas, #1) by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Odd Thomas</a> and Stephen King's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10589.Bag_of_Bones" title="Bag of Bones by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Bag of Bones</a>--but I think that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/456028.Red__Book_of_History_Chronicles_The_Circle___2_" title="Red (Book of History Chronicles The Circle, #2) by Ted Dekker" rel="nofollow noopener">Red</a> is the fourth or fifth Ted Dekker book that has made one of those mysterious beads of moisture well up in my eye.<br /><br />In Red, Thomas Hunter lives in both twenty-first century America and "Other Earth," which is regular Earth only about two millennia in the future. Every time he falls asleep in one world he awakens in the other. Current Earth is currently (ha-ha) undergoing a terrible crisis in which everyone on the planet has been infected with a lethal virus, and the people who hold the antivirus are using it as a political tool to gain world domination. (Reviewer's note: Please read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125956.Black__Books_of_History_Chronicles_The_Circle___1_" title="Black (Books of History Chronicles The Circle, #1) by Ted Dekker" rel="nofollow noopener">Black</a> first. Then you will know what I'm talking about.)<br /><br />In Other Earth, Thomas leads the Forest Dwellers against the evil desert-dwelling Horde who forsook Elyon's (God's) love. Each group wishes to obliterate the other, and each suffers heavy losses in battle. But a rogue warrior named Justin, formerly of the Forest Guard, wishes to make peace with the Horde. The Forest Dwellers think this is blasphemy and wish to put him to death. But Justin has many followers. He preaches a gospel of love and basically tells the Forest Dwellers they're a bunch of hypocrites because they're really no different from the Horde. <br /><br />Now here is where I think Thomas is a little clueless. In regular Earth he's the estranged son of an army chaplain, and if I had been in his shoes, I would have been like, "Yo, Justin. You're like the second coming of Christ. Far out!" But Thomas is as blind as the rest of the Forest Dwellers and even has a duel against Justin. (Guess who loses.)<br /><br />Anyway, those of you who know what happened to Jesus can probably guess what happens to Justin, only I think that Christ had the easier way out than Justin does. <br /><br />The thing about these books that moves me to the core is the way unconditional love plays so prominently in everything the characters do. The modern parallels with Scripture make me look at Christ in a new light. The gospel reading in church this past Sunday was Luke 4:21-30, where Jesus was speaking in the synagogue and made everyone so mad that they tried to hurl him off of a hilltop. People thought he was nuts! Just like the Forest Dwellers thought that Justin was nuts. And little does everyone know that the one they are persecuting is their own God!<br /><br />So yeah. I shed a tear. But it was a good tear.<br /><br />By the way, Dustin of Washington, I hope you're happy that I actually wrote a heartfelt, long-winded review this time around. :)<br /><br />Bailey out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7338601625665404555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40475304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40475304" />
    <a title="Jill Williamson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/955038-jill-williamson"><img alt="Jill Williamson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442498975p2/955038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40475304?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill Williamson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill Williamson" href="/user/show/955038-jill-williamson">Jill Williamson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/955038-jill-williamson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40475304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16122801403769202119">Thomas Hunter lay sleeping in a hotel room in Bangkok. Just as he’d predicted, the deadly The Raison Strain virus had been released into the world. His sister lets him sleep, though, for now.<br/><br/>In another reality, Thomas rides a black steed over a sandy valley, leading his Forest Guard to war against the Horde. Having eaten the fruit that blocks dreams, it’s been fifteen years since he last walked in Earth’s reality. This alternate world has become his home. But to defeat the Horde he needs an expl</span>
  <span id="freeText16122801403769202119" style="display:none">Thomas Hunter lay sleeping in a hotel room in Bangkok. Just as he’d predicted, the deadly The Raison Strain virus had been released into the world. His sister lets him sleep, though, for now.<br /><br />In another reality, Thomas rides a black steed over a sandy valley, leading his Forest Guard to war against the Horde. Having eaten the fruit that blocks dreams, it’s been fifteen years since he last walked in Earth’s reality. This alternate world has become his home. But to defeat the Horde he needs an explosive, something he can only get by going to sleep.<br /><br />He wakes in Bangkok to find a gun pressed to his temple, thus Thomas enters back into his bizarre dual reality, hoping to save two worlds from destruction. But he is only one man. Whatever happens to his body in one world happens to his body in the other. The things he learns in one world, he takes into the other. But what happens if he dies?<br /><br />Without an antivirus, everyone in the world will die from the Raison Strain within a few weeks. Monique, the scientist working on the antivirus, is kidnapped by the perpetrators who want to rule the world. As the terrorists demand the world surrender their nuclear weapons in exchange for the antivirus, Thomas Hunter works with the United States government to try to prevent the end of the world, and when he sleeps, Thomas is trying to save his people from an equally devastating crisis with the Horde. <br /><br />This story just keeps going and it’s very gripping. If you haven’t read the first novel, I suggest you start there, then get this one. Dekker snags the reader into this amazing journey with Thomas and doesn’t let up. The book has a bit of an ending, but like Black, Red leaves you hanging enough that you need to run to the bookstore to get a copy of White, the last book in the series. I highly recommend Red to anyone looking for a big adventure. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16122801403769202119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2363576693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363576693" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4605519-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319681755p2/4605519.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2363576693?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <span id="freeText3214374021151482350" style="display:none">I have a friend who loves these books and I hate that I rated it so low. The book is based on a fairly original idea. It makes some good points at times. I am a Christian and I know this trilogy is much loved by some people and I have no problem with it's underlying message or any point it tries to make. Thomas and his travails in 2 worlds just don't work for me.<br /><br />There are some good portions, some good (if slightly heavy handed) use of symbology... but the dialog is stilted, plot shaky, and the set up just doesn't hang together... I say this, and I love fantasy. Fantasy be it epic, medieval, urban or whatever is a genre I enjoy. I just found this one somewhat weak in the "story telling" department. <br /><br />I wish I could like this/these more. <br /><br />So, 2 stars and I hope White is better. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_495053264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495053264" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/742586-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304565511p2/742586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495053264?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/742586-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495053264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10857026876331304973">OK... let's start off with the good. There's an exciting pace and lots of adrenaline to this story. The pages turn quickly. It's one of those books where you get a nervous sweat going anticipating the next plot turn. Unfortunately, I had a lot of issues with many of those turns.<br/><br/>So if you're a huge fan of the author or the series, you should probably stop reading my review now, because it pretty much goes downhill from here. <br/><br/>I'm no stranger to suspending disbelief for a good story. Sentient robot</span>
  <span id="freeText10857026876331304973" style="display:none">OK... let's start off with the good. There's an exciting pace and lots of adrenaline to this story. The pages turn quickly. It's one of those books where you get a nervous sweat going anticipating the next plot turn. Unfortunately, I had a lot of issues with many of those turns.<br /><br />So if you're a huge fan of the author or the series, you should probably stop reading my review now, because it pretty much goes downhill from here. <br /><br />I'm no stranger to suspending disbelief for a good story. Sentient robots, magical elves, blood-sucking fiends, talking animals, indestructible supermen... I'm pretty much on board for anything. But the story has to have logical rules that allow me to suspend disbelief. So whenever I hit a passage or scenario where rules of logic (even as crazily defined by the world in the story) are completely disregarded or nonexistent.... it REALLY, REALLY, REALLY annoys me. <br /><br />Unfortunately, that happened far too many times in this story, the second in a trilogy, wherein our hero spends time between two very different worlds every time he goes to sleep.<br /><br />First of all, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ creating black powder as an explosive (all the way from exploring, mining, distillation and refinement of all the raw materials!) in a couple hour period while a horde of 10,000 warriors waits at the bottom of a canyon under tons of rock surfaces, which are conveniently looming, yet fragile enough to be dislodged by a couple dozen packed black powder bombs? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> LUDICROUS! Think about it, if <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the horde was close enough to be crushed by said tons of rock, wouldn't they also be close enough to see people scrambling around on the cliff faces? <br /><br />"Hey, what are those guys doing underneath that looming cliff which could fall down and crush us? Hmm... I dunno. I'm sure it's nothing. Let's get back to screaming and stomping around in a menacing way without really moving too far from under these tons of precariously placed rock." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Second, in the modern world, the virus-terrorist demands <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that all countries ship their nuclear weapons to France, to be under said virus-terrorist control. LUDICROUS! As if all these nuclear weapons were able to packed up and shipped off like a bunch of fruits and vegetables. And as if they would have any actual use once disconnected from their delivery and support systems. Yes, yes, I know the author makes some clarifications about how they are are going to just dump most of them in the sea next to their base of operations, but what sense does that even make? Why would you want your base of operations sitting next to a sea full of submerged nuclear warheads? What happens when/if a little sea water seeps in and corrodes all of those sensitive electronic parts?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Maybe that's all part of the future plot line to be resolved later.<br /><br />But perhaps most unforgivable and illogical is when our hero <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and second in command sneak into the horde compound to steal the holy history books. They make their way through the commander's tent, killing his general along the way. Then, INSTEAD OF KILLING the horde commander, they tiptoe around his sleeping form, realize there are too many history books to carry off in one go, and sneak back out again, saying they'll have to come back later to get all the books. LUDICROUS! Killing the main bad guy would've been the optimal thing to do here... except he probably needs to make an appearance later in the story, so the author had to devise a way to keep him around. And the guy they DID kill is later passed off as a redshirt, not a general, because I think the author later realized he should have kept him around.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />So, so very frustrating.<br /><br />I'm completely put off by the religious zealotry of our hero in the "old" world. Our hero feels that the horde, if they do not individually accept the word of Elyon (i.e., accept him as their personal lord/savior) should be destroyed. In other words, up to a certain plot turn that comes later, he's totally cool with the murder every non-believing man, woman and child. That sounds a bit too much like fanatical Islam (the Taliban) for me to get on board. But as distasteful as that is, it's worse (from a "logical/rules of the story" viewpoint) that his religious zealotry doesn't follow him into the "new" world when he makes the sleepover switch, although allegedly he's the same person. So on our side, he's NOT a religious zealot, but just a guy trying to stop a virus from destroying humanity. If the logic was consistent, his religious zealotry WOULD translate over, and then he'd probably be trying to use the virus to destroy every man, woman and child who doesn't accept Elyon as lord and savior... which I guess would be everyone in our world. <br /><br />Finally, the story is wrapped up in the end of the book by a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ religi-psycho-babble-almalgam of Christianity martyrdom inspiring what, at arm's length, one could interpret as mass suicide - if not for the magic of baptism/rebirthing that occurs afterward. It all seems written just to tug at the heartstrings of Christian folk. Ick!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />... and yet I am probably going to continue reading this series into the third book. <br /><br />WHAT IS WRONG WITH ME?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10857026876331304973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_294486276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/294486276" />
    <a title="M.G. Edwards" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5625318-m-g-edwards"><img alt="M.G. Edwards" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442518523p2/5625318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294486276?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.G. Edwards" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.G. Edwards" href="/user/show/5625318-m-g-edwards">M.G. Edwards</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294486276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3205587608082698963">Author Ted Dekker offers an interesting premise in his Circle Trilogy (Black/Red/White) -- that a man can alternate between the present and the future through his dreams and influence one reality by his actions in the other. The series is also a fascinating Biblical allegory. The final book, White, is the best of the three, because it explains clearly in the finale most of the unanswered questions Dekker raises in this thought-provoking series. For fans of fantasy, speculative fiction, and Chris</span>
  <span id="freeText3205587608082698963" style="display:none">Author Ted Dekker offers an interesting premise in his Circle Trilogy (Black/Red/White) -- that a man can alternate between the present and the future through his dreams and influence one reality by his actions in the other. The series is also a fascinating Biblical allegory. The final book, White, is the best of the three, because it explains clearly in the finale most of the unanswered questions Dekker raises in this thought-provoking series. For fans of fantasy, speculative fiction, and Christian literature, it's a real treat. It's smart writing with undertones that make you think.<br /><br />The story is a bit melodramatic at times and lags in places, and it's difficult to keep the multitude of characters straight because some lack depth or disappear and reappear at different points in the trilogy. You also have to suspend belief when Dekker writes about how politics in Washington and foreign governments work. It's not the way geopolitics works.<br /><br />All in all, it's a trilogy worth reading. I gave the first two books, Black and Red, four stars primarily because at times they leave the reader confused about names, places, events, and how they relate to the Biblical allegory. In the end, though, Dekker redeems himself with a solid ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3205587608082698963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_220799480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220799480" />
    <a title="Kasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia"><img alt="Kasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494441972p2/2087548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220799480?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kasia" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia">Kasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220799480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18391222559961048855">The second installment of the Circle Trilogy did not disappoint but managed to choke me even more than "Black" - the first book that everyone should read prior to experiencing "Red". It has been a long, long time since a book made me tear up and this roused up with emotions and abyssal feelings that only very skilled writers can exude from their reader. This is a fascinating installment that takes Thomas Hunter, the man who lives in our reality when awake and also in another world when he dreams</span>
  <span id="freeText18391222559961048855" style="display:none">The second installment of the Circle Trilogy did not disappoint but managed to choke me even more than "Black" - the first book that everyone should read prior to experiencing "Red". It has been a long, long time since a book made me tear up and this roused up with emotions and abyssal feelings that only very skilled writers can exude from their reader. This is a fascinating installment that takes Thomas Hunter, the man who lives in our reality when awake and also in another world when he dreams at nigh, on the wildest ride of his life. This can only be described as a new form of allegory; characters who understand our world are reflected in the dream world which is engulfed in a battle of massive proportions, people are no longer standing for an idea, they are someone else in the other world and if they die then those consequences spill over and threaten everything that Thomas and his sister ever knew.<br /><br />America is in the hot seat with the release and spread of a deadly virus, and Thomas must use his dreams to find answers and ways to stop it before he is eradicated and he can dream no more. Those who oppose him want him dead and want his dreams to stop but others who love life have nothing left but the hope that he can save them - easier said than done, Ted Dekker likes to swing his heroes and foes as deep as his mind allows, and this is one hairy book, it takes a lot of sweat and guts to take this ride.<br /><br />In the dream world those who rejected Elyon's waters have turned to Desert Dwellers known as Scabs, dry and disease stricken nomads, their minds and eyes are ashen with sickness and visions of death and conquests, the worship Teeleh and the Shataiki and will stop at nothing until the remaining forests and their people are destroyed. In real life Thomas is on hot pursuit to find and rescue the one person who can stop the Raison Virus; the creator of the vaccine herself - Monique de Raison. Her role in the story is much deeper than the reader might think of and I actually guessed part of her secret, it felt amazing thought to live with the characters are see how they developed and how some changed for better and some for worse. Carlos and other mercenaries of death are on hot pursuit and the reader is in for a delicious treat of intrigue, some romance and countless twists and turns.<br /><br />In this book Ted Dekker writes an ultimate showdown between good and evil, and it's been done to the death in books and movies but this novel is simply astounding. I read it in two days and would have read it in one sitting if I wasn't sick with a bad cold, it was truly a book that I know will stay with me forever and I am simply dying to read the last installment "White". These books are so deep and moving they are impossible to describe in a review, instead they should be enjoyed like a fine meal, one that serves more than one purpose to feed, it enriches the user forever and I feel blessed to have taken this journey with Dekker and his friends and foes. So please enjoy and take away from the riches that make the heart beat faster and the head spin - these books read like nothing else and are extremely satisfying.<br /><br />- Kasia S. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18391222559961048855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2811836351331276173">Thomas Hunter lay sleeping in a hotel room in Bangkok. Just as he’d predicted, the deadly The Raison Strain virus had been released into the world. His sister lets him sleep, though, for now.<br/><br/>In another reality, Thomas rides a black steed over a sandy valley, leading his Forest Guard to war against the Horde. Having eaten the fruit that blocks dreams, it’s been fifteen years since he last walked in Earth’s reality. This alternate world has become his home. But to defeat the Horde he needs an expl</span>
  <span id="freeText2811836351331276173" style="display:none">Thomas Hunter lay sleeping in a hotel room in Bangkok. Just as he’d predicted, the deadly The Raison Strain virus had been released into the world. His sister lets him sleep, though, for now.<br /><br />In another reality, Thomas rides a black steed over a sandy valley, leading his Forest Guard to war against the Horde. Having eaten the fruit that blocks dreams, it’s been fifteen years since he last walked in Earth’s reality. This alternate world has become his home. But to defeat the Horde he needs an explosive, something he can only get by going to sleep.<br /><br />He wakes in Bangkok to find a gun pressed to his temple, thus Thomas enters back into his bizarre dual reality, hoping to save two worlds from destruction. But he is only one man. Whatever happens to his body in one world happens to his body in the other. The things he learns in one world, he takes into the other. But what happens if he dies?<br /><br />Without an antivirus, everyone in the world will die from the Raison Strain within a few weeks. Monique, the scientist working on the antivirus, is kidnapped by the perpetrators who want to rule the world. As the terrorists demand the world surrender their nuclear weapons in exchange for the antivirus, Thomas Hunter works with the United States government to try to prevent the end of the world, and when he sleeps, Thomas is trying to save his people from an equally devastating crisis with the Horde. <br /><br />This story just keeps going and it’s very gripping. If you haven’t read the first novel, I suggest you start there, then get this one. Dekker snags the reader into this amazing journey with Thomas and doesn’t let up. The book has a bit of an ending, but like Black, Red leaves you hanging enough that you need to run to the bookstore to get a copy of White, the last book in the series. I highly recommend Red to anyone looking for a big adventure. </span>

<div id="review_399690970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/399690970" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12194068-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345857938p2/12194068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/399690970?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/12194068-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer399690970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5476676372628116210">Note: this review treats the whole series, of which this book is a part. No spoilers.<br/><br/>All in all, a bit disappointing. Dekker's strength is suspense; he kept me wanting to know what happened enough to read the whole series (Black, Red, White, Green) pretty quickly (~1600 pages). In the end, though, I'm not sure it was worth the time. He isn't a very good writer, his plots are predictable, the Christian imagery is a bit heavy-handed (extremely so at times), and aspects of the story went beyond my </span>
  <span id="freeText5476676372628116210" style="display:none">Note: this review treats the whole series, of which this book is a part. No spoilers.<br /><br />All in all, a bit disappointing. Dekker's strength is suspense; he kept me wanting to know what happened enough to read the whole series (Black, Red, White, Green) pretty quickly (~1600 pages). In the end, though, I'm not sure it was worth the time. He isn't a very good writer, his plots are predictable, the Christian imagery is a bit heavy-handed (extremely so at times), and aspects of the story went beyond my suspension of disbelief. He also steals unreservedly from C.S. Lewis but lacks Lewis' talent or creativity, so if you've read Lewis first, you're bound to be disappointed. However, Dekker's themes are heavy enough and his underlying theology strong enough that portions of the series could spark serious discussion if used in the right way. I cried several times, not because the writing was that good, but because the story (Jesus and redemption) is that good. It is one of Dekker's goals to retell that greatest of stories in all his books, and this he does consistently. For this, I'd give it 2 1/2 stars if I could.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5476676372628116210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2402030864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402030864" />
    <a title="Neil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11192244-neil"><img alt="Neil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435376678p2/11192244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402030864?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil" href="/user/show/11192244-neil">Neil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780849917912" href="/book/show/924293.Red">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=end-of-the-world">end-of-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=finished-in-2018">finished-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11192244-neil?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402030864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9300669921084978947">It is interesting reading this for a second time [considering the first time was when it first came out]. It moves at a pretty good clip. It also has a bit of a 'time gap' in it where Hunter's "story" [life?] in the alternate reality starts back up fifteen years after the events in the first book whereas the events in "our reality" start up where the first book leaves off. It has excitement, action, adventure, romance, mystery, violence, "mysticism," religious elements, and elements of fantasy a</span>
  <span id="freeText9300669921084978947" style="display:none">It is interesting reading this for a second time [considering the first time was when it first came out]. It moves at a pretty good clip. It also has a bit of a 'time gap' in it where Hunter's "story" [life?] in the alternate reality starts back up fifteen years after the events in the first book whereas the events in "our reality" start up where the first book leaves off. It has excitement, action, adventure, romance, mystery, violence, "mysticism," religious elements, and elements of fantasy and sci-fi. The character development is interesting, as you have the main characters from the "prime reality" kind-of growing as the book progresses and the characters from the "alternate reality" developing even further [due to the that reality being "fifteen years later"]. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought it was an interesting take on Jesus' crucifixion and resurrection. In the alternate reality, there are frequent references to Biblical [Christian] principles and beliefs [which I was fine with], but presented from a 'different perspective.' I thought the author did a great job presenting some Christian beliefs from a different point-of-view [such as "dying on the cross" - in the alternate reality, it is "drowning in the water" to live for Justin]. You have the innocent man dying [the only innocent man on the planet] for the sins of everybody so that everybody might truly live and be free from the evil/wickedness inside.<br /><br />It was also interesting to read about how the ones that the boy saved from the first book became legalistic over time and had become distracted from "The Great Romance." There were six to ten major laws about how to live out "The Great Romance," and yet, the Forest Dwellers felt the need to tack on numerous other laws to further spell out how to correctly "follow" "The Great Romance." This made the Great Romance a bunch of legalism that did little to change the hearts of the Forest Dwellers; actually, it made the Forest Dwellers more like the Desert Dwellers than they wanted to admit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was interesting to read about Monique and Carlos "experiencing" Hunter's "alternate reality" in different ways. I thought it was pretty crazy how Carlos suddenly developed a cut on his neck mimicking the cut on Martyn's [Johan's] neck. It will be interesting to see how much Johan matches up with Carlos in the third book. Monique "matches" up with Rachelle, despite neither woman looking like each other. There was a scar on Carlos' face that matched a scar on Johan's face, which led Hunter to believe Carlos and Johan might be somehow linked between the two realities. It will be interesting to see how much this progresses in the third book [if more poeple cross over between the two realities]. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It has been interesting reading this book. There are times I am, "No, you idiot! Don't do that!" while reading because it seems pretty obvious to me [the reader] that the character [mostly Thomas Hunter] is making a really bad, incredibly stupidly bad, decision, with no means of stopping. It is kind of funny, in a way. Also, the book does not veer off into familiar territory that other books might go. The author tends to take different paths of resolution; there are times I am thinking "the only good bug is a dead bug!" but he takes a different tact. The author has violence in his story, but there is a "purpose" to it; it is not violence for the sake of violence. The violence, while not being obnoxiously graphic, helps move the story along. I was surprised at how often I found myself expecting the author to resort to violence and being surprised ["disappointed"] that a different method was found. I think the author showed there is a time and place for violence in these novels; I also think the author helped show that as Christians we are to continually think spiritually about life around us. To think spiritually might not necessarily mean taking the easiest option; it might mean taking a harder choice that is more difficult in the short term but has "greater dividends" in the long run. <br /><br />On a side note, parts of the book really reminded me of his <i>Mortal</i> series of books. Both books had deserts, inhabitants transformed by sin/wickedness/selfishness, people continually seeking "deeper truths" and being transformed by what they discovered, and followers continually turning against their leaders. Both series also talk about legalism versus "freedom" when it comes to Christianity [as represented in each book]. Followers believe they have received 'the final revelation' but become the very thing they 'hate' because they stop loving and start judging those who are different, who are sinful, who need help. The comment is made throughout this book that even though the Forest Dwellers claim they love Elyon, their hearts and attitudes indicate otherwise. They worship a religion. a "format" to follow, instead of the person [founder/Creator] behind the religion. I know I say these books remind me of aspects of the <i>Mortals</i> books, but that is only because it has been over fifteen years since I read <i>The Circle</i> series whereas I read the other series in the last year or so. <br /><br />I do think this book is filled with wonderful allegories of the redemptive and healing power(s) of Jesus via Justin. Just as in 'real life,' the heroes do not always get the answer that they want to their prayers or heart's desire(s). It is interesting, too, because the followers of Elyon are constantly reminded to "guard their hearts" and to "guide their hearts" instead of letting their hearts and emotions guide them. This is a valuable lesson that needs to be learned "today" and to be reminded of daily. <br /><br />I would say most of this book focuses on "the other reality" as opposed to "our reality." The first book jumps back and forth more between the two realities; this one, not so much. That is okay, considering the "time gap" between the first book and the second book for the 'alternate reality.' It will be interesting to see how the third book plays out. <br /><br />There were some parts in this book that made me groan and cringe internally. Not because of the violence or whatnot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[More because of how the scene played out. For example, Hunter is sent in to rescue Monique with a team of US Special Forces operators. The airplane in which they are flying is shot down via a heat-seaking missile; Hunter is the only one to survive. It was really disappointing, because I would have loved to have seen how he interacted with a batch of bad-to-the-bone American soldiers instead of them being redshirted so fast. In that respect, it was painful. hahahah There were a few moments in "the other reality" that had me cringing because it seemed like Thomas was being obviously, painfully stupid while being completely oblivious to the consequences to his bad [poor] decisions. But, that is okay. That is the direction the author chose to go and probably mimics "real life" more than I realize.<br /><br />It is funny, but this is clearly not <i>Mission Impossible</i> or some other story where the heroes know every step they are going to take and how it will play out in order to always make the right decision. This book mimics "real life" in terms of how a person can watch a friend or loved one make bull-headed decisions while walking right off a proverbial cliff and not be able to do anything to prevent that friend or loved one from making bad decisions. Such moments as these occur quite a bit in the story. It was frustrating, but that helped give the book a 'freshness' that other books may not have.<br /><br />I did find myself wondering how much the books would change, if they were written "today" due to the advances in technology. For example, instead of having soldiers circling a mountain until their airplane was shot from the sky, drones could have been sent in to look for the "telltale" heat signatures. Modern technology and science has advanced quite a bit in the past decade or so; I can only imagine how he might have utilized them in his stories. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I thought the author did a great job with this second book in the series. I felt the writing, storytelling, and descriptions [characters] were better [stronger] than in the first book. Even thought it does seem to slow down in parts, it still moves along at a good clip. It held my interest throughout the entire book, and I had a hard time putting it down. It was a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9300669921084978947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14402133464636122952">As good as his first in the series is Red pushes the envelope to another level. There's more action, more suspense and the clock winds down ever closer before the global pandemic destroys most of the world.<br/><br/>Whereas the first book covers the fall of man in allegorical fashion the second novel focuses on the redemption of man. After the fall of man a sickness descended upon the dream world which can only be cured by ritual washing in special water created by Elyon. Thomas is a leader of those who c</span>
  <span id="freeText14402133464636122952" style="display:none">As good as his first in the series is Red pushes the envelope to another level. There's more action, more suspense and the clock winds down ever closer before the global pandemic destroys most of the world.<br /><br />Whereas the first book covers the fall of man in allegorical fashion the second novel focuses on the redemption of man. After the fall of man a sickness descended upon the dream world which can only be cured by ritual washing in special water created by Elyon. Thomas is a leader of those who chose to remain under Elyon's blessing and wash in the waters and he leads a group of soldiers who fight against those cursed with the sickness - the Horde. In our world Thomas fights against an assassin to rescue the one woman capable of synthesising a vaccine for the airborne virus threatening humankind. Political intrigue is created in this story as the nations discuss how to deal with this terrorism scare. <br /><br />The most interesting facet of all books to me is what conflict is formed. Here in Red romantic, political, mental and physical conflict exists in abundance and help carry the story to another level than in Black. Dekker's subtitle for Red is the heroic rescue, however I believe it could easily also be the renewing. For this book is not just focussed on the renewal of humanity but is a renewal of the story begun in Black.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14402133464636122952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_100082711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100082711" />
    <a title="Devin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3638874-devin"><img alt="Devin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342094708p2/3638874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100082711?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devin" href="/user/show/3638874-devin">Devin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781595547316" href="/book/show/6226346-red">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3638874-devin?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3638874-devin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer100082711&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100082711" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15289622578421304942">In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125956.Black__The_Circle___1_' title='Black (The Circle, #1) by Ted Dekker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black</a>, I was introduced to an exciting story littered with allusions to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1441.Ted_Dekker' title='Ted Dekker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ted Dekker</a>'s Pentecostal theology. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/456028.Red__The_Circle___2_' title='Red (The Circle, #2) by Ted Dekker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red</a>, Dekker presents a very clear redemptive analogy in the more fantastic of the two worlds in this book. Dekker emphasizes Arminian, free-will salvation at every turn. Dekker goes so far as to have the "Jesus" character tell his followers that they are "cured" (ultimately) because they choose to obey him. Also, Dekker's view on the bridegroom-bride relationship between Jesus and the</span>
  <span id="freeText15289622578421304942" style="display:none">In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125956.Black__The_Circle___1_" title="Black (The Circle, #1) by Ted Dekker" rel="nofollow noopener">Black</a>, I was introduced to an exciting story littered with allusions to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1441.Ted_Dekker" title="Ted Dekker" rel="nofollow noopener">Ted Dekker</a>'s Pentecostal theology. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/456028.Red__The_Circle___2_" title="Red (The Circle, #2) by Ted Dekker" rel="nofollow noopener">Red</a>, Dekker presents a very clear redemptive analogy in the more fantastic of the two worlds in this book. Dekker emphasizes Arminian, free-will salvation at every turn. Dekker goes so far as to have the "Jesus" character tell his followers that they are "cured" (ultimately) because they choose to obey him. Also, Dekker's view on the bridegroom-bride relationship between Jesus and the church is rather simple and almost shallow. Dekker only meets theology on a level that positively engages the emotions, going no further.<br /><br />However, this book is quite an emotional ride, and this is largely why I have enjoyed The Circle Series so far. Dekker is a brilliant writer. I just wish he could be considered, in some measure, a theologian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15289622578421304942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2764002571190803272">2nd book in the Circle Trilogy by Ted Dekker. It continues the epic saga of Thomas Hunter in a thrilling, but bloody, read.   <span id="freeText2764002571190803272" style="display:none">2nd book in the Circle Trilogy by Ted Dekker. It continues the epic saga of Thomas Hunter in a thrilling, but bloody, read. The allegorical undertones are more prevalent in this book, as Dekker makes the character representing Christ very evident. <br /><br />Of the 3 books in the trilogy, this one would be filled with the most action and battles. The romance aspect is not as emphasized as the 1st or 3rd books. After finishing this book, you will want to have the 3rd book (White) on-hand, so you can continue the journey uninterrupted. Dekker knows how to capture his readership!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B+cRXk28Y+R+3J38vdvAo0W9Dnki76lqDG+L3yovJP5AwTtN2wmB6YI1BaweZv3vw6z2jAS54DF9xJAiQuJUlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Harris contends that one must begin with a new attitude, viewing love, purity, and singleness from God\'s perspective rather than thinking that love and romance are to be enjoyed &quot;solely for recreation.&quot; In such well-named chapters as &quot;Guarding Your Heart&quot; and &quot;What Matters at Fifty,&quot; Harris encourages the reader to look at one\'s character rather than reveling in infatuation, to regard love as a truly selfless, biblical act rather than a feeling. He refutes the concept that we are victims of &quot;falling in love&quot; (that it is beyond our control), saying that &quot;God wants us to seek guidance from scriptural truth, not feeling. Smart love looks beyond personal desires and the gratification of the moment.
